                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Performance of the HC||NFM pouch cell. a) Long-term cycling performance of the 3Ah HC||NFM pouch cell at 1&nbsp;C. b) Rate performance, c) discharge cures at low temperatures, and d) cycle performance at 50&nbsp;°C. e) Comparison of the performance of practical HC-based SIBs modified by electrolytes, as reported in the past five years.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202405319-sec-0090">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202405319-sec-0090-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, we have successfully designed an AN-based electrolyte tailored for practical and versatile SIBs using a top-down approach. AN was selected as the primary solvent due to its optimal combination of viscosity, dielectric constant, Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient, transference number, electrochemical stability window, and desolvation energy. By partially replacing AN with the diluent OTE, a unique solvation shell enriched with FSI⁻ anions was created, leading to an inorganic-rich, highly stable electrode-electrolyte interface. This innovative electrolyte enables the HC electrode to deliver a significantly higher specific capacity of 223 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 5&nbsp;C, while the HC||NVP full cell exhibits stable cycling for 2500 cycles with a capacity retention of 79.1%. Moreover, the electrolyte shows broad compatibility with various cathode materials, as evidenced by the stable cycling performance of the HC||NFM full cell. At a high cut-off voltage of 4.15 V, the cell retains 82.0% of its capacity after 1400 cycles at a high rate of 5&nbsp;C. More importantly, the practicality of the electrolyte was verified in a 3 Ah pouch cell, which retains 90.7% of its capacity after 1000 cycles. Additionally, the designed electrolyte enables the pouch cell to deliver reliable performance within the temperature range of −60 to 50&nbsp;°C. This work provides a promising pathway for the development of advanced electrolytes for SIBs capable of delivering high power and dependable performance in diverse environmental conditions.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="aenm202405319-sec-0100">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202405319-sec-0100-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202405319-sec-0110">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202405319-sec-0120">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202405319-sec-0130">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="aenm202405319-sec-0130-title"> Electrolyte and Electrode Preparation</h4>
                  
                  <p>The 1M-AN electrolyte consists of 1 M NaFSI dissolved in AN. The 1M-AN/OTE electrolyte comprises 1 M NaFSI dissolved in a mixture of AN and OTE at a volume ratio of 4:6. The carbonate-based NP186 electrolyte contains 1 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> dissolved in a 3:7 (v/v) mixture of EC and DEC. The ether-based NP035 electrolyte comprises 1 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> dissolved in DME. All electrolytes and salts were provided by Suzhou Duoduo Chemical Technology Co., Ltd., with a purity greater than 99.8%, and were used as received.</p>
                  
                  <p>HC electrodes were prepared by casting a slurry composed of 90% HC active material (Type 2, Kuraray Co., Ltd.), 5% Super P as the conductive agent, and 5% sodium alginate (Shanghai HUSHI Co., Ltd.) as the binder onto Al foil. The NVP electrode, coated on Al foil, was prepared from a slurry containing 85% active material, 5% Super P, and 10% polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF, KF Polymer, KUREHA Co., Ltd.) as the binder. Except for adjusting the ratio of active material, conductive agent, and binder to 90:5:5, the preparation method of the NFM electrode was identical to that of the NVP electrode. For HC||NVP full cells, the average mass loading of the HC and NVP active materials was 3.8 mg cm<sup>−2</sup> and 8−10 mg cm⁻<sup>2</sup>, respectively. For HC||NFM full cells, the average mass loading of the HC and NFM active materials was 4.8 and 8 mg cm<sup>−2</sup>, respectively. For the Na-free three-electrode batteries, the HC electrode had a mass loading of 1.8 mg cm⁻<sup>2</sup>. The 50SOC-NVP electrode was prepared according to the previously reported method.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405319-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405319-bib-0021_R_d69773515e1420" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Sci. China Chem.">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The pre-dried electrode was punched into 12 mm diameter discs, further dried in a vacuum oven at 80&nbsp;°C, and transferred to a glovebox (Mikrouna Co., Ltd.) filled with high-purity argon (Ar), where water and oxygen levels were maintained below 0.1 ppm.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202405319-sec-0140">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="aenm202405319-sec-0140-title"> Battery Configurations</h4>
                  
                  <p>CR2016 coin-type full cells were assembled using the as-prepared NVP or NFM electrode as the cathode, HC as the anode, glass fiber (Whatman GF/C) as the separator, and 70 µL of electrolyte. The Na-metal-free NVP||HC||50SOC-NVP cell was evaluated using a Swagelok-type configuration based on a three-electrode protocol. In this setup, the HC electrode served as the working electrode (WE), a freshly prepared NVP electrode with more than twice the capacity of the HC electrode was used as the counter electrode (CE), and a precycled 50SOC-NVP electrode functioned as the reference electrode (RE). The cell was assembled with 450 µL of electrolyte. Detailed design parameters for the pouch cell can be found in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a> (Supporting Information).</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202405319-sec-0150">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="aenm202405319-sec-0150-title"> Electrochemical Measurements</h4>
                  
                  <p>The rate performance of the HC anode was evaluated using a Na-metal-free NVP||HC||50SOC-NVP cell. After a single formation cycle at 0.1&nbsp;C (1&nbsp;C = 300 mA g<sup>−1</sup>), the cell underwent five charge-discharge cycles at gradually increasing rates of 0.2&nbsp;C, 0.5&nbsp;C, 1&nbsp;C, 2&nbsp;C, 3&nbsp;C, 4&nbsp;C, and 5&nbsp;C, and finally returned to 0.5&nbsp;C. The voltage range was set between −1.38 and −3.38 V versus 50SOC-NVP, which can be conveniently converted to the Na<sup>+</sup>/Na scale by adding 3.38 V, corresponding to 0–2 V (vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na). The performance tests of the three-electrode batteries were carried out on the LANHE battery test system (CT-3002A-5V10mA, Wuhan, China), a more detailed description of the Na-free three-electrode testing protocol can be found in the previous work.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405319-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405319-bib-0021_R_d69773515e1453" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Sci. China Chem.">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The electrochemical performance of the assembled HC||NVP and HC||NFM full cells was evaluated using the Neware battery test system (CT-4008Tn-5V10mA, Shenzhen, China) after being held for 4 h. All batteries were activated at a current rate of 0.1&nbsp;C (1&nbsp;C = 117 mA g<sup>−1</sup> for HC||NVP and 1&nbsp;C = 150 mA g<sup>−1</sup> for HC||NFM) for three cycles. For coin-type full cells, the HC||NVP cells were cycled within a voltage range of 1.5–3.9 V, while the HC||NFM cells operated within a voltage range of 1.5–4.15 V. The cycling stability of the HC||NVP full cells was evaluated after the formation cycles at a 1&nbsp;C or 5C rate. The rate capability of HC||NVP batteries was tested at increasing charging and discharging rates of 5&nbsp;C, 6&nbsp;C, 7&nbsp;C, 8&nbsp;C, 9&nbsp;C, 10&nbsp;C, 11&nbsp;C, 12&nbsp;C, 13&nbsp;C, 14&nbsp;C and 15&nbsp;C, 5 cycles were performed at each current rate. The high-rate cycling stability of the HC||NFM full cells was evaluated at a 5&nbsp;C rate. The cycling performance of the 3 Ah HC||NFM pouch cell was evaluated through charge-discharge tests at 1&nbsp;C (1&nbsp;C = 3 A) within the voltage range of 1.5–3.85 V. Specifically, after formation cycles at 0.05&nbsp;C and 0.1&nbsp;C, the cell was charged at 1&nbsp;C to 3.85 V with constant current, followed by constant voltage charging with a cut-off current of 0.05&nbsp;C and then discharged at 1&nbsp;C to 1.5 V under constant current, with this protocol repeated continuously. For assessing low-temperature performance, the cell was first charged at 0.1&nbsp;C at room temperature and then tested for constant current discharge at 0.1&nbsp;C at various temperatures, including −20, −30, −40, −50, and −60&nbsp;°C. The in situ EIS measurements were performed using a Princeton electrochemical workstation on HC||NVP cells within a voltage range of 2–3.5 V to prevent interference from cathode electrode interphase (CEI) film formation on NVP at high cut-off potential. The cells were cycled at 0.5&nbsp;C, and EIS spectra were collected every three cycles at 3.5 V, with a total of 26 spectra recorded. The EIS tests were conducted with an alternating current (AC) amplitude of 10 mV over a frequency range from 100 kHz to 0.1 Hz.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202405319-sec-0160">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="aenm202405319-sec-0160-title"> Materials Characterizations</h4>
                  
                  <p>The surface composition of the SEI on HC electrodes was examined through XPS using a Thermo Scientific K-α spectrometer equipped with monochromatic Al Kα radiation (excitation energy = 1468.6 eV). The <sup>23</sup>Na NMR spectra for electrolytes were captured using a 500 MHz Bruker NMR spectrometer (Switzerland) at ambient temperature, with deuterium oxide (D<sub>2</sub>O) serving as the locking field substance within a coaxial NMR tube. 0.5 <span class="smallCaps">m</span> sodium chloride (NaCl) in D<sub>2</sub>O electrolyte was employed as an internal reference within the same tube. Raman spectroscopy was conducted using an XploRA Raman microscope (HORIBA Jobin Yvon, France) with a 532 nm laser. The melting point and boiling point of the electrolytes were determined by differential scanning calorimetry (DSC) using a NETZSCH 200 F3 Maia instrument.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202405319-sec-0170">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="aenm202405319-sec-0170-title"> Theoretical Oxidation/Reduction Potential Calculations</h4>
                  
                  <div class="paragraph-element">To calculate the oxidation potential and reduction potential of solvent molecules, the geometry of different isolated solvent molecules was optimized in the gas phase using ORCA-5.0.4 software at the B3LYP/ma-def2-TZVP level using DFT.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405319-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405319-bib-0034_R_d69773515e1489" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - WIREs Comput Mol Sci">34</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Frequency calculations were also performed at the same level to obtain thermodynamic corrections, and the zero point energy (ZPE) was corrected using a factor of 0.986.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405319-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405319-bib-0035_R_d69773515e1494" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - J. Chem. Theory Comput.">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The oxidation potential <i>E<sub>ox</sub></i> (vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) can be calculated by the following formula:

                                                   <mi>A</mi>
                                                   <mo>−</mo>
                                                </msup>
                                             </mfenced>
                                             <mo>−</mo>
                                             <mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi>
                                             <mi>G</mi>
                                             <mfenced close=")" open="(">
                                                <mi>e</mi>
                                             </mfenced>
                                             <mo>−</mo>
                                             <mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi>
                                             <msub>
                                                <mi>G</mi>
                                                <mrow>
                                                   <mi>s</mi>
                                                   <mi>o</mi>
                                                   <mi>l</mi>
                                                </mrow>
                                             </msub>
                                             <mfenced close=")" open="(">
                                                <mi>A</mi>
                                             </mfenced>
                                          </mrow>
                                       </mfenced>
                                       <mi>F</mi>
                                    </mfrac>
                                    <mo linebreak="goodbreak">−</mo>
                                    <mn>1.73</mn>
                                 </mrow>
                                 <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{E_{re}}\;\left( A \right) = - \frac{{\left[ {\Delta G_{gas}^{re} + \Delta {G_{sol}}\left( {{A^ - }} \right) - \Delta G\left( e \right) - \Delta {G_{sol}}\left( A \right)} \right]}}{F} - 1.73\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                              </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(3)</span></div>
                     <div class="inline-equation" id="aenm202405319-disp-0004"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                           <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/305c2a2e-74be-4348-af5c-9f9bfbaa603c/aenm202405319-math-0006.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16146832:media:aenm202405319:aenm202405319-math-0006" display="block" location="graphic/aenm202405319-math-0006.png">
                              <semantics>
                                 <mrow>
                                    <mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi>
                                    <msubsup>
                                       <mi>G</mi>
                                       <mrow>
                                          <mi>g</mi>
                                          <mi>a</mi>
                                          <mi>s</mi>
                                       </mrow>
                                       <mrow>
                                          <mi>r</mi>
                                          <mi>e</mi>
                                       </mrow>
                                    </msubsup>
                                    <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                                    <msub>
                                       <mi>G</mi>
                                       <mrow>
                                          <mi>g</mi>
                                          <mi>a</mi>
                                          <mi>s</mi>
                                       </mrow>
                                    </msub>
                                    <mspace width="0.28em"></mspace>
                                    <mfenced close=")" open="(" separators="">
                                       <msup>
                                          <mi>A</mi>
                                          <mo>−</mo>
                                       </msup>
                                    </mfenced>
                                    <mo linebreak="goodbreak">−</mo>
                                    <msub>
                                       <mi>G</mi>
                                       <mrow>
                                          <mi>g</mi>
                                          <mi>a</mi>
                                          <mi>s</mi>
                                       </mrow>
                                    </msub>
                                    <mfenced close=")" open="(">
                                       <mi>A</mi>
                                    </mfenced>
                                 </mrow>
                                 <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}\Delta G_{gas}^{re} = {G_{gas}}\;\left( {{A^ - }} \right) - {G_{gas}}\left( A \right)\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                              </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(4)</span></div>where <i>G<sub>gas</sub></i>(<i>A</i><sup>−</sup>) corresponds to the Gibbs free energy for the reduced state state in the gas phase, Δ<i>G<sub>sol</sub></i>(<i>A</i><sup>−</sup>) corresponds to the solvation free energy for the reduced state.</div>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202405319-sec-0180">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="aenm202405319-sec-0180-title"> Classical Molecular Dynamics&nbsp;Simulations</h4>
                  
                  <p>cMD was conducted using the Gromacs 2020.6 software suite.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405319-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405319-bib-0038_R_d69773515e1825" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Comput. Phys. Commun.">38</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Molecular interactions were described by the General Amber Force Field (GAFF).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405319-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405319-bib-0039_R_d69773515e1830" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - J. Comput. Chem.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Atomic point charges were derived using the Restrained Electrostatic Potential (RESP) method and fitted with Multiwfn.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405319-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405319-bib-0040_R_d69773515e1835" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Commun. Chem. J. Comput. Chem.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Initial structures of the different systems were generated using the PACKMOL software package,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405319-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405319-bib-0041_R_d69773515e1841" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - J. Comput. Chem.">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> with Na<sup>+</sup>, FSI<sup>−</sup>, EC, PC, DMC, EMC, DEC, THF, DOL, DME, DIG, TMP, AN, and OTE molecules placed randomly in a 55&nbsp;×&nbsp;55&nbsp;×&nbsp;55 Å box according to the molar ratios shown in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> (Supporting Information). Initial energy minimization was performed using the steepest descent method. The system was then equilibrated in the isothermal-isobaric ensemble (NPT) for 20 ns using a V-rescale thermostat and Berendsen barostat, maintaining a temperature of 298.15 K and a pressure of 1 bar, with a time step of 0.5 fs. After equilibration, an additional 30 ns simulation was conducted using a Nosé-Hoover thermostat and Parrinello-Rahman barostat. The statistical analysis of the solvation structure was conducted using a self-written Python script developed with the MDAnalysis package.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405319-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405319-bib-0042_R_d69773515e1854" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - J. Comput. Chem.">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The last 5 ns of the simulation, comprising 10&nbsp;000 frames, were used for analysis. All visualizations were generated using the Visual Molecular Dynamics (VMD) program.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405319-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405319-bib-0043_R_d69773515e1859" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - J. Mol.Graph.">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
                  
                  <div class="paragraph-element">The self-diffusion diffusion coefficients <i>D</i> for Na<sup>+</sup> and FSI<sup>−</sup> were obtained by analysis of the mean square displacement (MSD) over time using the Einstein relation:<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405319-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405319-bib-0044_R_d69773515e1872" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - J. Phys. Chem. B">44</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup><div class="inline-equation" id="aenm202405319-disp-0005"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                           <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/a0ca4497-af0f-4515-ba99-8ef6557a2c97/aenm202405319-math-0007.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16146832:media:aenm202405319:aenm202405319-math-0007" display="block" location="graphic/aenm202405319-math-0007.png">
                              <semantics>
                                 <mrow>
                                    <mi>D</mi>
                                    <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                                    <munder>
                                       <mi>lim</mi>
                                       <mrow>
                                          <mi>t</mi>
                                          <mo>→</mo>
                                          <mi>∞</mi>
                                       </mrow>
                                    </munder>
                                    <mfrac>
                                       <mfenced close="〉" open="〈" separators="">
                                          <mrow>
                                             <mi>M</mi>
                                             <mi>S</mi>
                                             <mi>D</mi>
                                             <mfenced close=")" open="(">
                                                <mi>t</mi>
                                             </mfenced>
                                          </mrow>
                                       </mfenced>
                                       <mrow>
                                          <mn>6</mn>
                                          <mi>t</mi>
                                       </mrow>
                                    </mfrac>
                                    <mspace width="0.28em"></mspace>
                                 </mrow>
                                 <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}D = \mathop {\lim }\limits_{t \to \infty } \frac{{\left\langle {MSD\left( t \right)} \right\rangle }}{{6t}}\;\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                              </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(5)</span></div>where <i>MSD</i>(<i>t</i>) is the mean-square displacement of a molecule center of mass during time <i>t</i> and &lt; &gt; denotes an ensemble average.</div>
                  
                  <div class="paragraph-element">The Na<sup>+</sup> transference number in a binary dilute electrolyte solution, where both ions are monovalent (a 1:1 electrolyte), is determined by the diffusion rates of Na<sup>+</sup> and its counterion, as expressed by the following relationship:<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405319-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405319-bib-0045_R_d69773515e1920" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - ACS Energy Lett.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup><div class="inline-equation" id="aenm202405319-disp-0006"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                           <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/8308424c-2eca-4cbc-bf1b-377a3a82b072/aenm202405319-math-0008.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16146832:media:aenm202405319:aenm202405319-math-0008" display="block" location="graphic/aenm202405319-math-0008.png">
                              <semantics>
                                 <mrow>
                                    <msub>
                                       <mi>t</mi>
                                       <mrow>
                                          <mi>N</mi>
                                          <msup>
                                             <mi>a</mi>
                                             <mo>+</mo>
                                          </msup>
                                       </mrow>
                                    </msub>
                                    <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                                    <mfrac>
                                       <msub>
                                          <mi>D</mi>
                                          <mrow>
                                             <mi>N</mi>
                                             <msup>
                                                <mi>a</mi>
                                                <mo>+</mo>
                                             </msup>
                                          </mrow>
                                       </msub>
                                       <mrow>
                                          <msub>
                                             <mi>D</mi>
                                             <mrow>
                                                <mi>N</mi>
                                                <msup>
                                                   <mi>a</mi>
                                                   <mo>+</mo>
                                                </msup>
                                             </mrow>
                                          </msub>
                                          <mo>+</mo>
                                          <msub>
                                             <mi>D</mi>
                                             <mrow>
                                                <mi>F</mi>
                                                <mi>S</mi>
                                                <msup>
                                                   <mi>I</mi>
                                                   <mo>−</mo>
                                                </msup>
                                             </mrow>
                                          </msub>
                                       </mrow>
                                    </mfrac>
                                    <mspace width="0.28em"></mspace>
                                 </mrow>
                                 <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{t_{N{a^ + }}} = \frac{{{D_{N{a^ + }}}}}{{{D_{N{a^ + }}} + {D_{FS{I^ - }}}}}\;\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                              </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(6)</span></div> where <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/d0aa32ec-17e4-45b7-9e60-31d9500a0236/aenm202405319-math-0009.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16146832:media:aenm202405319:aenm202405319-math-0009" display="inline" location="graphic/aenm202405319-math-0009.png">
                        <semantics>
                           <mrow>
                              <mspace width="0.28em"></mspace>
                              <msub>
                                 <mi>t</mi>
                                 <mrow>
                                    <mi>N</mi>
                                    <msup>
                                       <mi>a</mi>
                                       <mo>+</mo>
                                    </msup>
                                 </mrow>
                              </msub>
                              <mspace width="0.28em"></mspace>
                           </mrow>
                           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$\;{t_{N{a^ + }}}\;$</annotation>
                        </semantics></math> is the Na<sup>+</sup> transference number, <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/f9ccf95c-984d-4983-8776-0b3525f7e821/aenm202405319-math-0010.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16146832:media:aenm202405319:aenm202405319-math-0010" display="inline" location="graphic/aenm202405319-math-0010.png">
                        <semantics>
                           <msub>
                              <mi>D</mi>
                              <mrow>
                                 <mi>N</mi>
                                 <msup>
                                    <mi>a</mi>
                                    <mo>+</mo>
                                 </msup>
                              </mrow>
                           </msub>
                           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${D_{N{a^ + }}}$</annotation>
                        </semantics></math> is the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient, and <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/a2d448d1-1b27-45ef-bcdc-7588385da182/aenm202405319-math-0011.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:16146832:media:aenm202405319:aenm202405319-math-0011" display="inline" location="graphic/aenm202405319-math-0011.png">
                        <semantics>
                           <mrow>
                              <mspace width="0.28em"></mspace>
                              <msub>
                                 <mi>D</mi>
                                 <mrow>
                                    <mi>F</mi>
                                    <mi>S</mi>
                                    <msup>
                                       <mi>I</mi>
                                       <mo>−</mo>
                                    </msup>
                                 </mrow>
                              </msub>
                           </mrow>
                           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$\;{D_{FS{I^ - }}}$</annotation>
                        </semantics></math> is the FSI<sup>−</sup> diffusion coefficient.</div>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="aenm202405319-sec-0190">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="aenm202405319-sec-0190-title"> Ab Initio Molecular Dynamics&nbsp;Simulations</h4>
                  
                  <p>Trajectory-averaged PDOS for 1M-AN and 1M-AN/OTE electrolytes were obtained from AIMD simulations. Initial electrolyte structures were generated using PACKMOL software by randomly placing Na<sup>+</sup>, FSI<sup>−</sup>, AN, and OTE, with their quantities based on molar ratios. In the periodic box of 1M-AN, there were 4 NaFSI and 77 AN molecules, while in the periodic box of 1M-AN/OTE, there are 4 NaFSI, 30 AN, and 11 OTE molecules. Periodic cubic simulation cells with edge lengths of 19.687 Å for 1M-AN and 19.157 Å for 1M-AN/OTE were used, determined by the measured mass densities. Simulations were performed using the CP2K/Quickstep software package with the Perdew–Burke–Ernzerhof (PBE) functional and canonical ensemble (NVT) at 298.15 K.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#aenm202405319-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="aenm202405319-bib-0046_R_d69773515e2030" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - J. Chem. Phys">46</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The double-ζ MOLOPT basis set (DZVP-MOLOPT-SR-GTH) and Goedecker–Teter–Hutter (GTH) pseudopotentials were utilized. The energy cutoff was set to 400 Ry, and the Self-Consistent Field (SCF) convergence was targeted at 1.0&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−6</sup>. Each electrolyte system underwent 15 ps of AIMD simulations with a 1.0 fs time step, where the solvation structure equilibrated within the first 10 ps. The PDOS was calculated every 50 fs, with the final 5 ps used to determine the trajectory-averaged PDOS.</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>

         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="aenm202405319-sec-0220-title"> Author Contributions</h2>
         
         <p>X.D. and Y.X. conceived and supervised the projects. X.D. and G.L. proposed the electrolyte design concepts and co-wrote the manuscript. G.L. performed the electrochemical measurements and theoretical calculations. K.Z. prepared the NFM electrodes. Y.C. provided the dry pouch cells. R.H. conducted the electrolyte ignition tests. G.L., K.Z., Y.C., R.H., Y.W., Y.X., and X.D. carried out the characterization experiments and data analysis. All authors contributed to the discussion of results and reviewed the manuscript.</p>
